X FOREWARD The publication of this work known as Srimad Bhagavadarchana prakarana will be hailed by all who wish to obtain the details of worhip of Vishnu as ordained in the Vaikhanasa sutrasред The volume contais the text giving con- cisely the details of such worship according to Vaikhanasa texets with a brief commentary which explains the various stages that follow one another in course of the worship and gives out fully all the Vedic Mantras to be uttered in each actред The text and the commentary are followed by certain pas- sages from authoritative treatises on the details of worship during noon and eveningsред Then come the expiatory rites to be observed in case of errors or unforeseen accidentsред The final section called the Anubandha or supplement is a run- ning commentary on the text itself explaining several terms and practices which require special treatment with authori- ties cited from the works of sages like Atri, Marichi, Bhrigu, etcред, The work in the present from enlightens even a lay man who stands outside the Vaikhanasa creed but is eager to learn the precise practices as ordained by the great sages and to make it a basis for the higher conceptions of philosophyред But the publication of the work is limited to the vaikhanasa sect to whom it is undoubtedly most welcome but it can be with adventage read by others for the research advancing in every branch of human knowledge is being purified by a compre- hensive and sympathetic view of ancient conceptions and their practices which contributed to the welfare of ancient nationsред The work presupposes the necessity of worshipping God in an idol form idol worship takes it basis on the fundamental principles of philosophy and psychologyред Ancient sages in laving down the canons of conduct had in their view four xi vital ideals of man for the achivement of which all his daily activities in life are concentrated and shaped accordinglyред These are called the purusharthas, Dharma, Artha, Kama and Mokshaред The first and the foremost of theseред vizред, the Dharma is, as inferred from the verious definitions given by several schools of thought, such a sacrifice of self, Artha and Kama as to ensure the up-keep of the general welfare of mankindред Artha is the material which is capable of maintaining a happy lifeред Kama is the pleasure given to sensesред Moksha is the an- nihilation of births and deathsред These four ideals of acquisi- tion embrace every just activity of man in a societyред Among the first three, no one ideal should be given preponderence at the expense of any other, ieред, acquisition of Artha at the sac- rifice of Dharma and Kama, of Kama at the expence of Artha or Dhramaред Such transgression in some cases affects the doer and in most cases the society as wellред The great sages have found means to acquire purusharthas seperately and unitedlyред In the case of the last purushartha Karma and Jnana are the two paths prescribed for its pursuitред There the darsanas differ But if their views are examined with a reconciliatory mood, the canons of each darsana can be followed by different adhikaris, iредeред, the fittest to follow themред That which teaches the most advanced stage is unfit for a beginner who has just placed his foot on the first step of the spiritual ladderред The darsana, which appeals to the majority of men, that is exclud- ing those who have almost reached the highest stage of yoga practices and are on the threshold of salvation, is most the beneficial for followersред The worship of Vishnu in idol-from was deemed by the stages to achieve the fourfold end of hu- man activities for the generality of menред Those who think that the universe is the Temple of God and His worship is not limited by either space or time can see God everywhere and at all times; in fact they are always in the presence of

! xii divinityред Then what about the others? Divine Being is shape- less, indefinatle; all-perveding seen only in effect; but the mind of man is limited in conceptions of time and spaceред How can the limited hold the unlimited? Then psychology creates such a conception of divinity as the mind is capable of concievingред But all minds are not equal in its capacityред Some have advanced to transfer every concrete idea into abstract and vice versa while others cannot think beyond a concrete ideaред Then for their benefite a concrete form endowed with the superhuman characterestics was found necessary for the ordinary minds to start with the idea of Divine Beingред Slowly his mind reaches higher and higher till he grasps the neture of the true devinityред That is a long ride in samsara which serves it as a mirror exposing the really og each stage of mental progressред Thus the idol-worship is justified by the sagesред Even those religionists who discard idols, do actually use before their minds and consequently show in thier actions, the concrete forms with various attributes, as the Saviour or Prophet lead- ing to blissред Their minds reach only the stage called savikalpaka samadhi and not what is called nirvikalpaka stateред Vishnu is chosen for worship in a concrete form; for the conception of his attributes lead to the achivement of all the four-fold desiresред The sages created the characterescstics of divine being according to the desires of each devotee limited by the advance of his mind towards divinityред A man desirous of achieveing the end of Kama alone wants such a Deity who is resplendent with charming beauty endowed with all the happiness that the dovotee imagines his best in the achivement of Kamaред The same phenominon can be applied to the other ends of manред Vishnu is endowed with sattva-nature, which has the power of self control and endurance, which lead to

xiii the unstinted happinessред The conception of other deities en- dows them with different charecterestics and consequently with different functions For the general welfare of man Vishnu who promises to lead us to the acquisition of all the four aims of life is the chiefest deityред In the worship of Vishnu three are two schools which hold differences of opinion in practiceред One is Vikhanasa school and the other is called Pancharatraред Both the schools have been in existence from time immemorialред But their chief dif- ference lies in the fact that the Vikhanasa from is based en- tirely on the Vedic rituals while Pacharatra has taken in some of the tantric formsред But both the school derive their author- ity from the Vedasред The Hindu religion is distinguished from any other one in the chief conception of the Vadasред as the sole pramanya (authority or cognisance) and all the sects who relie on Vedic authority inspite of their minor difference in the doctrines come under the common fold of Hinduismред Vaikhanasa ritual is perhaps older than the Pancharatra and advocates the worship of Vishnu in an idol formред When a cancrete form is imposed upon an abstract idea all the characteristics of that from which is thus imposed must be maintained in all purity to avoid any antithetic idea, dis- pelling the tissue created by the imposed formред this psycho- logical phase of maintaining the purity of the conceived form necessitates certain formalities, which in the language of the Agamas are called the ritualsред the failure of a single rite makes the conception defective and the mind of the devotee fails to concentrate on all the characteristics of the concrete form of the Divinityред In ancient days Vaikhanasa ritual was very common and references in literature attest to itред Below are given two in- stances from Dandin’s Avantisundari, the largest prose work
